	<script>
(function(){
let xfhtml = document.getElementById('XF');
function applySetting(settingName, settingOn, allowToggle){
	
	// Theme editor is enabled. Check for selected toggle, otherwise apply default
		if(allowToggle === 1){
			let choice = localStorage.getItem(settingName);
			if( (choice === 'on') || (!choice && (settingOn === 1)) ){
				xfhtml.classList.add(settingName);
			}
		} else if(settingOn === 1){
			xfhtml.classList.add(settingName);
		}
	
}

applySetting('focus-mobile-navigation-bar', 1, 1);


applySetting('focus-fluid', 0, 1);


applySetting('focus-grid', 0, 1);


applySetting('focus-sidebar-sticky', 0, 1);


applySetting('focus-sidebar-flip', 0, 1);





	let backgroundChoice = localStorage.getItem('xenfocusBackground-62');
	if(backgroundChoice){ xfhtml.setAttribute('data-focus-bg', '' + backgroundChoice + '');	} else { xfhtml.setAttribute('data-focus-bg', '4'); }

})();
</script>

	<div class="message-userContent lbContainer js-lbContainer "
		data-lb-id="post-5632120"
		data-lb-caption-desc="Namatikapi &middot; Nov 8, 2024 at 4:51 PM">

		

		<article class="message-body js-selectToQuote">
			
				
			

			<div itemprop="text">
				
					
	

		
			
		

		
	


				<div class="bbWrapper">I agree with the options above !<br />
EW Fantasy is good but it&#039;s not a very intimate sound because they are ensembles. I also think about Albion Solstice, Groth, Lores (for dark med inspired ambiant and texture) and Sonokenitic Fantasy (if you like working with phrases, and for &quot;light&quot; fantasy).<br />
You can also have some very nice solo intruments for a good price : Have audio&#039;s Rebec, bass recorder, crumhorn, Kantele are really not pricy, Nordik Folk Strings from Silence and Other sound, and the libraries of Stefano Macarelli for the voices (and many other stuff), in particular Prometheus and Atlantis 3.<br />
There is a nice free Irish Harp in the Komplet Start and a beautiful free grand Harp in Project Sam&#039;s free orchestra 2.<br />
More classic instruments can fit very well for medieval : simple mandolins, flutes, organs, voices can be very useful !<br />
Also note that some eastern intruments like the Oud can blend very well into medieval/fantasy inspired music.</div>
			

	

		
			
		

		
	

				
			</div>

			<div class="js-selectToQuoteEnd">&nbsp;</div>
			
				
			
		</article>

		

		
	</div>

<img src="data:image/svg+xml;charset=utf-8,%3Csvg xmlns%3D'http%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2F2000%2Fsvg' width='574' height='692' viewBox%3D'0 0 574 692'%2F%3E" data-src="https://data2.vi-control.net/attachments/137/137403-c01d60c80f89aedde89849f9af62a617.jpg?hash=wB1gyA-Jrt"

</blockquote>There are very few medieval instruments in it (an Hurdy Gurdy - not bad sounding, a fiddle that I don&#039;t really like, and some flutes, and the voices maybe). Dulcimers and luths are not medieval (they are asian or eastern instruments in that collection, not the medieval version, even if they can do the job). They are quite simple and variable in quality IMO.<br />
If you are looking for an Hurdy Gurdy there are some free ones around (at Sonokinetic for example)<br />
Personnal opinion : the new Chris Hein&#039;s hybrid winds has a very Howard Shore&#039;s sounding ! Maybe you can think about that option too <img src="/community/styles/default/xenforo/smilies/smile.png"  class="smilie" loading="lazy" alt=":)" title="Smile    :)" data-shortname=":)" /></div>

	<div class="message-userContent lbContainer js-lbContainer "
		data-lb-id="post-5632140"
		data-lb-caption-desc="Draco Solis &middot; Nov 8, 2024 at 5:23 PM">

		

		<article class="message-body js-selectToQuote">
			
				
			

			<div itemprop="text">
				
					
	

		
			
		

		
	


				<div class="bbWrapper">For what it&#039;s worth, I&#039;ve played around with Fantasy Orchestra and agree with others&#039; assessment of it. It surely is a good library and can be used to make a fantasy score really well. If you&#039;re just thinking Skyrim overworld, it can surely do that. Probably even an epic tavern-esque theme, if you get creative with it.<br />
<br />
But if you want something small-scale that can make actual traditional tavern/folk music, then no, it isn&#039;t good for that. And to be fair, even Nick Phoenix himself has said that it was never meant to be a competitor to the ERA series or the like. It&#039;s an alternate take on the orchestra, not a folk library.</div>
			

	

		
			
		

		
	

				
			</div>

			<div class="js-selectToQuoteEnd">&nbsp;</div>
			
				
			
		</article>

		<i class="fa--xf far fa-code "><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" role="img" aria-hidden="true" ><use href="/community/data/local/icons/regular.svg?v=1766960843#code"></use></svg></i>
	</a>

				</li>
			
			
			
				<li>
					<a href="/community/threads/best-fantasy-music-vst.157416/#post-5632150" rel="nofollow">
						#20
					</a>
				</li>
			
		</ul>
	</header>

							

							<div class="message-content js-messageContent">
							

								
									
	
	
	

								

								
									
	

	<div class="message-userContent lbContainer js-lbContainer "
		data-lb-id="post-5632150"
		data-lb-caption-desc="ChiefZika &middot; Nov 8, 2024 at 6:15 PM">

		

		<article class="message-body js-selectToQuote">
			
				
			

			<div itemprop="text">
				
					
	

		
			
		

		
	


				<div class="bbWrapper">For quiet medieval-ish music, I can recommend a few that haven&#039;t been mentioned here. Too many, perhaps. But I feel morally obligated to dump this info on you, so BEAR WITH ME!<br />
<br />
<b>Karoryfer</b> has a great fantasy collection. For the sake of brevity, I won&#039;t go into detail, but yes, I agree with the Doc that they have good stuff. Lovely tagelharpas.<br />
<br />
<b>Embertone&#039;s Recorders </b>is a really bangin&#039; collection. Gives you 5 recorder registers, from bass to sopranino. You might get also a special discount on it out of nowhere if you get <b>Ivory Wind</b> from them, which is a FREE recorder! If you&#039;re not hung on having true legato, though, the Kontakt Factory recorders are perfectly serviceable.<br />
<br />
You might want some kind of zither or a psaltery. <b>Loops de la Cr<a href="https://www.loopsdelacreme.com/subscribe" target="_blank" class="link link--external" rel="nofollow ugc noopener">è</a>me&#039;s Gipsy Zither</b> is lovely. You can also get a solid free psaltery from <b>Bolder Sounds</b> or Versilian Studio&#039;s <b>VCSL</b> collection. VCSL also has a lot of other acoustic instruments, including recorders. A dirt cheap psaltery can be purchased from <b>Xperimenta</b>, who also have a tasty <i>harpsichord</i>. While I&#039;m on the topic of keyboards, you can also get a solid <b>virginal</b> from Sampletekk.<br />
<br />
Harps. Gotta love harps. The free Irish harp in Komplete Start is quite good. The <b>Fairy Tale Harp</b> from Hephaestus Sounds has a good amount of &quot;dirt&quot; to it, and I&#039;m sure the new harp freebie from <b>Straight Ahead Samples</b> would work well too. A lyre could also work, and Unreal Instruments has a nice one in their free <b>Small Instruments Collection.</b><br />
<br />
A frame drum for percussion would be good too. There are tons of good free options, but my personal favorite is <b>Framedrum 22″</b>, available in the Pulse Store... the brushed articulation lets me pretend i&#039;m making weird medieval jazz. (Pro tip: use the <i>SnareBuzz</i> VST on your frame drums to get a cool bristly sound. That said, for other percussion instruments, just about anything is fair game and probably has a solid free option for it as well. Tambourines, triangles, bodhrans, whatever.)<br />
<br />
As for a fiddle, I&#039;d not only be looking into violin libraries but also <b>viola</b> libraries, as violas sound more like medieval vielles. Obviously an actual vielle would be ideal, but yeah. <b>8Dio&#039;s Deep Solo Viola</b> has the right character for it in my opinion... not an ideal option, but if you want a viola and also want to save money, it&#039;ll do the trick. Just don&#039;t use the normal legato... literally every other legato patch sounds better.<br />
<br />
For whistles/flutes, lots of good free options once again, but I really dig the control/variety you can get out of <b>O&#039;Malley&#039;s Irish Whistles</b>. Unreal Instruments has a great and very usable free set in their <b>Two Whistles</b> library too.<br />
<br />
If I knew I&#039;d buy/download all of these, regardless of the discounts I got, I&#039;d have invested in one of the larger packages like ERA II, Rinascimento, Goblinity, or Orcophony. The latter two are very nicely discounted right now actually. You would most definitely get material that overlaps with what i&#039;ve said, and it&#039;d likely be more cost-effective if you&#039;re serious about making fantasy music.<br />
<br />
But hey, if you need a cheap/free/niche addition to the cast, my list is here for you. I can maybe add a few louder instruments later but this post is long enough as is.</div>
			

	

		
			
		

		
	

				
			</div>

			<div class="js-selectToQuoteEnd">&nbsp;</div>
			
				
			
		</article>

<script>

(function(){
	let html = document.getElementById('XF');

	
		// Advanced search menu
		if(document.querySelector('.focus-search-advanced')){
			document.querySelector('.focus-search-advanced').addEventListener('click', e => {
				html.classList.toggle("focus-search-menu-active");
			});
		}
		// Show advanced search menu on focus
		document.querySelector('.focus-search-flex input').addEventListener('focus', e => {
			html.classList.add("focus-search-menu-active");
		});
		// Close advanced search menu on document click
		document.body.addEventListener("click", e => {
			let clickedEl = e.target.closest(".focus-wrap-search");
			if(clickedEl) return;
			html.classList.remove("focus-search-menu-active");
		});
	
	
	
		// xenfocus editor: open and close with data-xenfocus-editor
		
		let customizerTriggers = document.querySelectorAll("[data-xenfocus-editor]");
	
		customizerTriggers.forEach(t => {
			t.addEventListener("click", e => {
				e.preventDefault();
				let customizer = document.getElementById("xenfocus-customizer");
				if(customizer.open){
					customizer.close();
				} else {
					customizer.showModal();
				}
			});
		});
	
		
			// Change background-image
			
			let backgroundToggles = document.querySelectorAll(".focus-picker span");
			backgroundToggles.forEach(t => {
				t.addEventListener("click", e => {
					let styleid = html.getAttribute("data-style-id"),
						backgroundClass = e.currentTarget.getAttribute("data-focus-bg");
					
					html.setAttribute("data-focus-bg", backgroundClass);
					localStorage.setItem('xenfocusBackground-' + styleid + '', '' + backgroundClass + '');
				});
			});
					
			
		let customizerPanels = document.querySelectorAll(".focus-editor-panel");

		customizerPanels.forEach(p => {

			// Set :checked status of toggles depending on localstorage
			let settingName = p.getAttribute("data-setting"),
				settingDefault = p.getAttribute("data-setting-default"),
				settingChoice = localStorage.getItem(settingName);
			if(settingChoice === 'on'){
				p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','on');
			} else if(settingChoice === 'off') {
				p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','off');
			} else {
				if(settingDefault === 'on'){
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','on');
				} else{
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','off');
				}
			}

			// Set event listener so settings can be toggled
			p.addEventListener("click", e => {
				let settingStatus = p.getAttribute("data-setting-status");

				if(settingStatus === 'on'){
					html.classList.remove(settingName);
					localStorage.setItem(settingName, 'off');
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status', 'off');
				} else {
					html.classList.add(settingName);
					localStorage.setItem(settingName, 'on');
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status', 'on');
				}
			});
		});
	

})();

	

</script>

	<script>
(function(){
let xfhtml = document.getElementById('XF');
function applySetting(settingName, settingOn, allowToggle){
	
	// Theme editor is enabled. Check for selected toggle, otherwise apply default
		if(allowToggle === 1){
			let choice = localStorage.getItem(settingName);
			if( (choice === 'on') || (!choice && (settingOn === 1)) ){
				xfhtml.classList.add(settingName);
			}
		} else if(settingOn === 1){
			xfhtml.classList.add(settingName);
		}
	
}

applySetting('focus-mobile-navigation-bar', 1, 1);


applySetting('focus-fluid', 0, 1);


applySetting('focus-grid', 0, 1);


applySetting('focus-sidebar-sticky', 0, 1);


applySetting('focus-sidebar-flip', 0, 1);

})();

Fantasy genre is absolutely my favourite!!

	<div class="message-userContent lbContainer js-lbContainer "
		data-lb-id="post-5632120"
		data-lb-caption-desc="Namatikapi &middot; Nov 8, 2024 at 4:51 PM">

		

		<article class="message-body js-selectToQuote">
			
				
			

			<div itemprop="text">
				
					
	

		
			
		

		
	


				<div class="bbWrapper">I agree with the options above !<br />
EW Fantasy is good but it&#039;s not a very intimate sound because they are ensembles. I also think about Albion Solstice, Groth, Lores (for dark med inspired ambiant and texture) and Sonokenitic Fantasy (if you like working with phrases, and for &quot;light&quot; fantasy).<br />
You can also have some very nice solo intruments for a good price : Have audio&#039;s Rebec, bass recorder, crumhorn, Kantele are really not pricy, Nordik Folk Strings from Silence and Other sound, and the libraries of Stefano Macarelli for the voices (and many other stuff), in particular Prometheus and Atlantis 3.<br />
There is a nice free Irish Harp in the Komplet Start and a beautiful free grand Harp in Project Sam&#039;s free orchestra 2.<br />
More classic instruments can fit very well for medieval : simple mandolins, flutes, organs, voices can be very useful !<br />
Also note that some eastern intruments like the Oud can blend very well into medieval/fantasy inspired music.</div>
			

	

		
			
		

		
	

				
			</div>

			<div class="js-selectToQuoteEnd">&nbsp;</div>
			
				
			
		</article>

		

		
	</div>

</blockquote>There are very few medieval instruments in it (an Hurdy Gurdy - not bad sounding, a fiddle that I don&#039;t really like, and some flutes, and the voices maybe). Dulcimers and luths are not medieval (they are asian or eastern instruments in that collection, not the medieval version, even if they can do the job). They are quite simple and variable in quality IMO.<br />
If you are looking for an Hurdy Gurdy there are some free ones around (at Sonokinetic for example)<br />
Personnal opinion : the new Chris Hein&#039;s hybrid winds has a very Howard Shore&#039;s sounding ! Maybe you can think about that option too <img src="/community/styles/default/xenforo/smilies/smile.png"  class="smilie" loading="lazy" alt=":)" title="Smile    :)" data-shortname=":)" /></div>

							<div class="message-content js-messageContent">
							

								
									
	
	
	

								

								
									
	

	<div class="message-userContent lbContainer js-lbContainer "
		data-lb-id="post-5632140"
		data-lb-caption-desc="Draco Solis &middot; Nov 8, 2024 at 5:23 PM">

		

		<article class="message-body js-selectToQuote">
			
				
			

			<div itemprop="text">
				
					
	

		
			
		

		
	


				<div class="bbWrapper">For what it&#039;s worth, I&#039;ve played around with Fantasy Orchestra and agree with others&#039; assessment of it. It surely is a good library and can be used to make a fantasy score really well. If you&#039;re just thinking Skyrim overworld, it can surely do that. Probably even an epic tavern-esque theme, if you get creative with it.<br />
<br />
But if you want something small-scale that can make actual traditional tavern/folk music, then no, it isn&#039;t good for that. And to be fair, even Nick Phoenix himself has said that it was never meant to be a competitor to the ERA series or the like. It&#039;s an alternate take on the orchestra, not a folk library.</div>
			

	

		
			
		

		
	

				
			</div>

			<div class="js-selectToQuoteEnd">&nbsp;</div>
			
				
			
		</article>

	<section class="message-user"

		<ul class="message-attribution-main listInline ">
			
			
			
			<li class="u-concealed">

		data-xf-init="copy-to-clipboard"
		data-copy-text="&lt;div class=&quot;js-xf-embed&quot; data-url=&quot;https://vi-control.net/community&quot; data-content=&quot;post-5632150&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;script defer src=&quot;https://vi-control.net/community/js/xf/external_embed.js?_v=30c63a64&quot;&gt;&lt;/script&gt;"
		data-success="Embed code HTML copied to clipboard."
		class="">
		<i class="fa--xf far fa-code "><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" role="img" aria-hidden="true" ><use href="/community/data/local/icons/regular.svg?v=1766960843#code"></use></svg></i>
	</a>

				<li>
					<a href="/community/threads/best-fantasy-music-vst.157416/#post-5632150" rel="nofollow">
						#20

							<div class="message-content js-messageContent">
							

								
									
	
	
	

								

								
									
	

	<div class="message-userContent lbContainer js-lbContainer "
		data-lb-id="post-5632150"
		data-lb-caption-desc="ChiefZika &middot; Nov 8, 2024 at 6:15 PM">

		

		<article class="message-body js-selectToQuote">
			
				
			

			<div itemprop="text">
				
					
	

		
			
		

		
	


				<div class="bbWrapper">For quiet medieval-ish music, I can recommend a few that haven&#039;t been mentioned here. Too many, perhaps. But I feel morally obligated to dump this info on you, so BEAR WITH ME!<br />
<br />
<b>Karoryfer</b> has a great fantasy collection. For the sake of brevity, I won&#039;t go into detail, but yes, I agree with the Doc that they have good stuff. Lovely tagelharpas.<br />
<br />
<b>Embertone&#039;s Recorders </b>is a really bangin&#039; collection. Gives you 5 recorder registers, from bass to sopranino. You might get also a special discount on it out of nowhere if you get <b>Ivory Wind</b> from them, which is a FREE recorder! If you&#039;re not hung on having true legato, though, the Kontakt Factory recorders are perfectly serviceable.<br />
<br />
You might want some kind of zither or a psaltery. <b>Loops de la Cr<a href="https://www.loopsdelacreme.com/subscribe" target="_blank" class="link link--external" rel="nofollow ugc noopener">è</a>me&#039;s Gipsy Zither</b> is lovely. You can also get a solid free psaltery from <b>Bolder Sounds</b> or Versilian Studio&#039;s <b>VCSL</b> collection. VCSL also has a lot of other acoustic instruments, including recorders. A dirt cheap psaltery can be purchased from <b>Xperimenta</b>, who also have a tasty <i>harpsichord</i>. While I&#039;m on the topic of keyboards, you can also get a solid <b>virginal</b> from Sampletekk.<br />
<br />
Harps. Gotta love harps. The free Irish harp in Komplete Start is quite good. The <b>Fairy Tale Harp</b> from Hephaestus Sounds has a good amount of &quot;dirt&quot; to it, and I&#039;m sure the new harp freebie from <b>Straight Ahead Samples</b> would work well too. A lyre could also work, and Unreal Instruments has a nice one in their free <b>Small Instruments Collection.</b><br />
<br />
A frame drum for percussion would be good too. There are tons of good free options, but my personal favorite is <b>Framedrum 22″</b>, available in the Pulse Store... the brushed articulation lets me pretend i&#039;m making weird medieval jazz. (Pro tip: use the <i>SnareBuzz</i> VST on your frame drums to get a cool bristly sound. That said, for other percussion instruments, just about anything is fair game and probably has a solid free option for it as well. Tambourines, triangles, bodhrans, whatever.)<br />
<br />
As for a fiddle, I&#039;d not only be looking into violin libraries but also <b>viola</b> libraries, as violas sound more like medieval vielles. Obviously an actual vielle would be ideal, but yeah. <b>8Dio&#039;s Deep Solo Viola</b> has the right character for it in my opinion... not an ideal option, but if you want a viola and also want to save money, it&#039;ll do the trick. Just don&#039;t use the normal legato... literally every other legato patch sounds better.<br />
<br />
For whistles/flutes, lots of good free options once again, but I really dig the control/variety you can get out of <b>O&#039;Malley&#039;s Irish Whistles</b>. Unreal Instruments has a great and very usable free set in their <b>Two Whistles</b> library too.<br />
<br />
If I knew I&#039;d buy/download all of these, regardless of the discounts I got, I&#039;d have invested in one of the larger packages like ERA II, Rinascimento, Goblinity, or Orcophony. The latter two are very nicely discounted right now actually. You would most definitely get material that overlaps with what i&#039;ve said, and it&#039;d likely be more cost-effective if you&#039;re serious about making fantasy music.<br />
<br />
But hey, if you need a cheap/free/niche addition to the cast, my list is here for you. I can maybe add a few louder instruments later but this post is long enough as is.</div>
			

	

		
			
		

		
	

				
			</div>

			<div class="js-selectToQuoteEnd">&nbsp;</div>

<script>

(function(){
	let html = document.getElementById('XF');

	
		// Advanced search menu
		if(document.querySelector('.focus-search-advanced')){
			document.querySelector('.focus-search-advanced').addEventListener('click', e => {
				html.classList.toggle("focus-search-menu-active");
			});
		}
		// Show advanced search menu on focus
		document.querySelector('.focus-search-flex input').addEventListener('focus', e => {
			html.classList.add("focus-search-menu-active");
		});
		// Close advanced search menu on document click
		document.body.addEventListener("click", e => {
			let clickedEl = e.target.closest(".focus-wrap-search");
			if(clickedEl) return;
			html.classList.remove("focus-search-menu-active");
		});
	
	
	
		// xenfocus editor: open and close with data-xenfocus-editor
		
		let customizerTriggers = document.querySelectorAll("[data-xenfocus-editor]");
	
		customizerTriggers.forEach(t => {
			t.addEventListener("click", e => {
				e.preventDefault();
				let customizer = document.getElementById("xenfocus-customizer");
				if(customizer.open){
					customizer.close();
				} else {
					customizer.showModal();
				}
			});
		});
	
		
			// Change background-image
			
			let backgroundToggles = document.querySelectorAll(".focus-picker span");
			backgroundToggles.forEach(t => {
				t.addEventListener("click", e => {
					let styleid = html.getAttribute("data-style-id"),
						backgroundClass = e.currentTarget.getAttribute("data-focus-bg");
					
					html.setAttribute("data-focus-bg", backgroundClass);
					localStorage.setItem('xenfocusBackground-' + styleid + '', '' + backgroundClass + '');
				});
			});
					
			
		let customizerPanels = document.querySelectorAll(".focus-editor-panel");

		customizerPanels.forEach(p => {

			// Set :checked status of toggles depending on localstorage
			let settingName = p.getAttribute("data-setting"),
				settingDefault = p.getAttribute("data-setting-default"),
				settingChoice = localStorage.getItem(settingName);
			if(settingChoice === 'on'){
				p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','on');
			} else if(settingChoice === 'off') {
				p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','off');
			} else {
				if(settingDefault === 'on'){
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','on');
				} else{
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','off');
				}
			}

			// Set event listener so settings can be toggled
			p.addEventListener("click", e => {
				let settingStatus = p.getAttribute("data-setting-status");

				if(settingStatus === 'on'){
					html.classList.remove(settingName);
					localStorage.setItem(settingName, 'off');
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status', 'off');
				} else {
					html.classList.add(settingName);
					localStorage.setItem(settingName, 'on');
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status', 'on');
				}
			});
		});
	

})();

	

</script>

	<script>
(function(){
let xfhtml = document.getElementById('XF');
function applySetting(settingName, settingOn, allowToggle){
	
	// Theme editor is enabled. Check for selected toggle, otherwise apply default
		if(allowToggle === 1){
			let choice = localStorage.getItem(settingName);
			if( (choice === 'on') || (!choice && (settingOn === 1)) ){
				xfhtml.classList.add(settingName);
			}
		} else if(settingOn === 1){
			xfhtml.classList.add(settingName);
		}
	
}

applySetting('focus-mobile-navigation-bar', 1, 1);


applySetting('focus-fluid', 0, 1);


applySetting('focus-grid', 0, 1);


applySetting('focus-sidebar-sticky', 0, 1);


applySetting('focus-sidebar-flip', 0, 1);





	let backgroundChoice = localStorage.getItem('xenfocusBackground-62');
	if(backgroundChoice){ xfhtml.setAttribute('data-focus-bg', '' + backgroundChoice + '');	} else { xfhtml.setAttribute('data-focus-bg', '4'); }

})();
</script>

	<div class="message-userContent lbContainer js-lbContainer "
		data-lb-id="post-5632120"
		data-lb-caption-desc="Namatikapi &middot; Nov 8, 2024 at 4:51 PM">

		

		<article class="message-body js-selectToQuote">
			
				
			

			<div itemprop="text">
				
					
	

		
			
		

		
	


				<div class="bbWrapper">I agree with the options above !<br />
EW Fantasy is good but it&#039;s not a very intimate sound because they are ensembles. I also think about Albion Solstice, Groth, Lores (for dark med inspired ambiant and texture) and Sonokenitic Fantasy (if you like working with phrases, and for &quot;light&quot; fantasy).<br />
You can also have some very nice solo intruments for a good price : Have audio&#039;s Rebec, bass recorder, crumhorn, Kantele are really not pricy, Nordik Folk Strings from Silence and Other sound, and the libraries of Stefano Macarelli for the voices (and many other stuff), in particular Prometheus and Atlantis 3.<br />
There is a nice free Irish Harp in the Komplet Start and a beautiful free grand Harp in Project Sam&#039;s free orchestra 2.<br />
More classic instruments can fit very well for medieval : simple mandolins, flutes, organs, voices can be very useful !<br />
Also note that some eastern intruments like the Oud can blend very well into medieval/fantasy inspired music.</div>
			

	

		
			
		

		
	

				
			</div>

			<div class="js-selectToQuoteEnd">&nbsp;</div>
			
				
			
		</article>

		

		
	</div>

</blockquote>There are very few medieval instruments in it (an Hurdy Gurdy - not bad sounding, a fiddle that I don&#039;t really like, and some flutes, and the voices maybe). Dulcimers and luths are not medieval (they are asian or eastern instruments in that collection, not the medieval version, even if they can do the job). They are quite simple and variable in quality IMO.<br />
If you are looking for an Hurdy Gurdy there are some free ones around (at Sonokinetic for example)<br />
Personnal opinion : the new Chris Hein&#039;s hybrid winds has a very Howard Shore&#039;s sounding ! Maybe you can think about that option too <img src="/community/styles/default/xenforo/smilies/smile.png"  class="smilie" loading="lazy" alt=":)" title="Smile    :)" data-shortname=":)" /></div>

	<div class="message-userContent lbContainer js-lbContainer "

		<article class="message-body js-selectToQuote">
			
				
			

			<div itemprop="text">
				
					
	

		
			
		

		
	


				<div class="bbWrapper">For what it&#039;s worth, I&#039;ve played around with Fantasy Orchestra and agree with others&#039; assessment of it. It surely is a good library and can be used to make a fantasy score really well. If you&#039;re just thinking Skyrim overworld, it can surely do that. Probably even an epic tavern-esque theme, if you get creative with it.<br />
<br />
But if you want something small-scale that can make actual traditional tavern/folk music, then no, it isn&#039;t good for that. And to be fair, even Nick Phoenix himself has said that it was never meant to be a competitor to the ERA series or the like. It&#039;s an alternate take on the orchestra, not a folk library.</div>
			

	

		
			
		

		
	

				
			</div>

			<div class="js-selectToQuoteEnd">&nbsp;</div>
			
				
			
		</article>

		<ul class="message-attribution-main listInline ">

							<div class="message-content js-messageContent">
							

								
									
	
	
	

								

								
									
	

	<div class="message-userContent lbContainer js-lbContainer "
		data-lb-id="post-5632150"
		data-lb-caption-desc="ChiefZika &middot; Nov 8, 2024 at 6:15 PM">

		

		<article class="message-body js-selectToQuote">
			
				
			

			<div itemprop="text">
				
					
	

		
			
		

		
	


				<div class="bbWrapper">For quiet medieval-ish music, I can recommend a few that haven&#039;t been mentioned here. Too many, perhaps. But I feel morally obligated to dump this info on you, so BEAR WITH ME!<br />
<br />
<b>Karoryfer</b> has a great fantasy collection. For the sake of brevity, I won&#039;t go into detail, but yes, I agree with the Doc that they have good stuff. Lovely tagelharpas.<br />
<br />
<b>Embertone&#039;s Recorders </b>is a really bangin&#039; collection. Gives you 5 recorder registers, from bass to sopranino. You might get also a special discount on it out of nowhere if you get <b>Ivory Wind</b> from them, which is a FREE recorder! If you&#039;re not hung on having true legato, though, the Kontakt Factory recorders are perfectly serviceable.<br />
<br />
You might want some kind of zither or a psaltery. <b>Loops de la Cr<a href="https://www.loopsdelacreme.com/subscribe" target="_blank" class="link link--external" rel="nofollow ugc noopener">è</a>me&#039;s Gipsy Zither</b> is lovely. You can also get a solid free psaltery from <b>Bolder Sounds</b> or Versilian Studio&#039;s <b>VCSL</b> collection. VCSL also has a lot of other acoustic instruments, including recorders. A dirt cheap psaltery can be purchased from <b>Xperimenta</b>, who also have a tasty <i>harpsichord</i>. While I&#039;m on the topic of keyboards, you can also get a solid <b>virginal</b> from Sampletekk.<br />
<br />
Harps. Gotta love harps. The free Irish harp in Komplete Start is quite good. The <b>Fairy Tale Harp</b> from Hephaestus Sounds has a good amount of &quot;dirt&quot; to it, and I&#039;m sure the new harp freebie from <b>Straight Ahead Samples</b> would work well too. A lyre could also work, and Unreal Instruments has a nice one in their free <b>Small Instruments Collection.</b><br />
<br />
A frame drum for percussion would be good too. There are tons of good free options, but my personal favorite is <b>Framedrum 22″</b>, available in the Pulse Store... the brushed articulation lets me pretend i&#039;m making weird medieval jazz. (Pro tip: use the <i>SnareBuzz</i> VST on your frame drums to get a cool bristly sound. That said, for other percussion instruments, just about anything is fair game and probably has a solid free option for it as well. Tambourines, triangles, bodhrans, whatever.)<br />
<br />
As for a fiddle, I&#039;d not only be looking into violin libraries but also <b>viola</b> libraries, as violas sound more like medieval vielles. Obviously an actual vielle would be ideal, but yeah. <b>8Dio&#039;s Deep Solo Viola</b> has the right character for it in my opinion... not an ideal option, but if you want a viola and also want to save money, it&#039;ll do the trick. Just don&#039;t use the normal legato... literally every other legato patch sounds better.<br />
<br />
For whistles/flutes, lots of good free options once again, but I really dig the control/variety you can get out of <b>O&#039;Malley&#039;s Irish Whistles</b>. Unreal Instruments has a great and very usable free set in their <b>Two Whistles</b> library too.<br />
<br />
If I knew I&#039;d buy/download all of these, regardless of the discounts I got, I&#039;d have invested in one of the larger packages like ERA II, Rinascimento, Goblinity, or Orcophony. The latter two are very nicely discounted right now actually. You would most definitely get material that overlaps with what i&#039;ve said, and it&#039;d likely be more cost-effective if you&#039;re serious about making fantasy music.<br />
<br />
But hey, if you need a cheap/free/niche addition to the cast, my list is here for you. I can maybe add a few louder instruments later but this post is long enough as is.</div>
			

	

		
			
		

		
	

				
			</div>

			<div class="js-selectToQuoteEnd">&nbsp;</div>
			
				
			
		</article>

		

		
	</div>

<script>

(function(){
	let html = document.getElementById('XF');

	
		// Advanced search menu
		if(document.querySelector('.focus-search-advanced')){
			document.querySelector('.focus-search-advanced').addEventListener('click', e => {
				html.classList.toggle("focus-search-menu-active");
			});
		}
		// Show advanced search menu on focus
		document.querySelector('.focus-search-flex input').addEventListener('focus', e => {
			html.classList.add("focus-search-menu-active");
		});
		// Close advanced search menu on document click
		document.body.addEventListener("click", e => {
			let clickedEl = e.target.closest(".focus-wrap-search");
			if(clickedEl) return;
			html.classList.remove("focus-search-menu-active");
		});
	
	
	
		// xenfocus editor: open and close with data-xenfocus-editor
		
		let customizerTriggers = document.querySelectorAll("[data-xenfocus-editor]");
	
		customizerTriggers.forEach(t => {
			t.addEventListener("click", e => {
				e.preventDefault();
				let customizer = document.getElementById("xenfocus-customizer");
				if(customizer.open){
					customizer.close();
				} else {
					customizer.showModal();
				}
			});
		});
	
		
			// Change background-image
			
			let backgroundToggles = document.querySelectorAll(".focus-picker span");
			backgroundToggles.forEach(t => {
				t.addEventListener("click", e => {
					let styleid = html.getAttribute("data-style-id"),
						backgroundClass = e.currentTarget.getAttribute("data-focus-bg");
					
					html.setAttribute("data-focus-bg", backgroundClass);
					localStorage.setItem('xenfocusBackground-' + styleid + '', '' + backgroundClass + '');
				});
			});
					
			
		let customizerPanels = document.querySelectorAll(".focus-editor-panel");

		customizerPanels.forEach(p => {

			// Set :checked status of toggles depending on localstorage
			let settingName = p.getAttribute("data-setting"),
				settingDefault = p.getAttribute("data-setting-default"),
				settingChoice = localStorage.getItem(settingName);
			if(settingChoice === 'on'){
				p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','on');
			} else if(settingChoice === 'off') {
				p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','off');
			} else {
				if(settingDefault === 'on'){
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','on');
				} else{
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status','off');
				}
			}

			// Set event listener so settings can be toggled
			p.addEventListener("click", e => {
				let settingStatus = p.getAttribute("data-setting-status");

				if(settingStatus === 'on'){
					html.classList.remove(settingName);
					localStorage.setItem(settingName, 'off');
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status', 'off');
				} else {
					html.classList.add(settingName);
					localStorage.setItem(settingName, 'on');
					p.setAttribute('data-setting-status', 'on');
				}
			});
		});
	

})();

	

</script>
